style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: Greek <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a><sup id="cite_ref-LGTS_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGTS-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> WAD<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fraport_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fraport Greece (page does not exist)">Fraport Greece</a><sup id="cite_ref-fraport-greece.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraport-greece.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Thessaloniki Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>SKG</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LGTS</b>), officially <b>Thessaloniki Airport "Makedonia"</b><sup id="cite_ref-ypa.gr_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypa.gr-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x9a\xcf\x81\xce\xb1\xcf\x84\xce\xb9\xce\xba\xcf\x8c\xcf\x82 \xce\x91\xce\xb5\xcf\x81\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xce\xbc\xce\xad\xce\xbd\xce\xb1\xcf\x82 \xce\x98\xce\xb5\xcf\x83\xcf\x83\xce\xb1\xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\xce\xaf\xce\xba\xce\xb7\xcf\x82 "\xce\x9c\xce\xb1\xce\xba\xce\xb5\xce\xb4\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\xce\xaf\xce\xb1"</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="el-Latn" title="Greek-language romanization">Kratik\xc3\xb3s Aerolim\xc3\xa9nas Thessalon\xc3\xadkis "Makedon\xc3\xada"</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-ypaEL_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypaEL-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and formerly <b>Mikra Airport</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> serving <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, the second-largest city in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. It is located 13&#160;km (8.1&#160;mi) southeast of the city, in <a href="/wiki/Thermi" title="Thermi">Thermi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LGTS_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGTS-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport is the third-largest airport in the country after <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heraklion_International_Airport" title="Heraklion International Airport">Heraklion International Airport</a>. It opened in 1930 and was the second-busiest airport in Greece in terms of flights served and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Greece" title="List of the busiest airports in Greece">third-busiest in terms of passengers</a> served in 2016, with over 6 million passengers. It is the main airport of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Greece" title="Northern Greece">Northern Greece</a> and apart from the city of Thessaloniki it also serves the popular tourist destination of <a href="/wiki/Chalkidiki" title="Chalkidiki">Chalkidiki</a> and the surrounding cities of <a href="/wiki/Central_Macedonia" title="Central Macedonia">Central Macedonia</a>. The Athens\xe2\x80\x93Thessaloniki route is <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_passenger_air_routes#Busiest_air_routes_inside_the_EU,_Switzerland,_Iceland_and_Norway_*" title="List of busiest passenger air routes">the tenth busiest in the EU</a> with 1.8 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> To cope with demand, a second terminal is currently under construction as part of a billion-euro investment by Fraport Greece, the company which operates the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-Naftemporiki_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naftemporiki-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fraport-profile_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraport-profile-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Facilities"><span apron</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Airlines_and_destinations"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Airlines and destinations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Overview"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Overview</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Annual_statistics"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Annual statistics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Busiest_passenger_routes_by_country"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Busiest passenger routes by country</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Busiest_routes"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Busiest routes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Top_airlines"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Top airlines</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Public_transport"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public transport</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Accidents_and_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The airport was first established as an <a href="/wiki/Airfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Airfield">airfield</a> during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">allied war effort</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_front" title="Macedonian front">Macedonian front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> There were numerous airfields at the time, including <em>Little Mikra</em>, <em>Big Mikra</em> (which became the current international airport), and the major military airfield of <a href="/wiki/Sedes_Air_Base" title="Sedes Air Base">Sedes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The first international flight to Thessaloniki landed at the <em>Little Mikra</em> air field, and government efforts at encouraging the growth of civil aviation saw the start of construction of a purpose-built civilian airport at the present location in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Works were temporarily abandoned due to the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> and the airport opened to civilian traffic in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Major works were undertaken after the war. The accession of Greece to <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a> saw NATO-funded investments such as the expansion of the 10/28 runway to 2,440 metres (8,010&#160;ft) and the inauguration of a new terminal building in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Damage to the tower caused by the <a href="/wiki/1978_Thessaloniki_earthquake" title="1978 Thessaloniki earthquake">1978 Thessaloniki earthquake</a> meant it needed to be torn down, and a new tower, still in operation, was built.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Modernisation works were undertaken in the late 1990s, as part of the celebrations for Thessaloniki being <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 1993 the airport took the name <em>Makedonia</em> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x9c\xce\xb1\xce\xba\xce\xb5\xce\xb4\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\xce\xaf\xce\xb1</span>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(Greece)" title="Macedonia (Greece)">Macedonia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The operational aspects of the airport were privatised in 2015. <a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport AG</a>/Copelouzos Group joint venture and <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Republic_Asset_Development_Fund" title="Hellenic Republic Asset Development Fund">the state privatisation fund</a> agreed to the privatisation of the airport operations, and 13 other Greek airports, in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Fraport Greece will operate the airport for 40 years starting on 11 April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-about_the_company_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about_the_company-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It pledged to invest \xe2\x82\xac400 million ($451.88 million) on the various airports, including a refurbishment of the existing terminal at Thessaloniki as well as the construction of a second terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-future_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-future-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Construction on the new terminal began on 19 September 2018<sup id="cite_ref-Naftemporiki_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naftemporiki-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and finished in February 2021, three months ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Fraport expects passenger traffic to increase by 48% by 2026 as a result of its investment.<sup id="cite_ref-parallaxi_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallaxi-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal">Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">airport\'s terminal</a> consists of three floors. The ground floor serves arrivals only and is divided into two sections: international/extra-Schengen arrivals and domestic/intra-Schengen arrivals. The second floor serves departures and also includes a shopping center. On this floor there are 34 check-in counters, waiting areas, bars, stores and various airlines\' offices. The third floor houses two restaurants and several bars with views to the runways. There are two passenger lounges. An additional terminal has opened in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-ypodomes_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypodomes-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways_and_apron">Runways and apron</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Runways and apron">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg/220px-Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg/330px-Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg/440px-Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thessaloniki_Airport_Aerial_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the airport in 2011, showing the progress of construction of the runway expansion</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport has two <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> (10/28 and 16/34) and two <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiways</a>. There are 22 stands for <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrow-body aircraft</a> and about 20 for <a href="/wiki/Light_aircraft" title="Light aircraft">light aircraft</a>.\n</p><p>A modernisation and expansion project for runway 10/28 began in 2005, with an initial completion date of 2011, but has since been delayed<sup id="cite_ref-ypodomes_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypodomes-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and was finally completed in March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Modernisation projects on the tarmac and other runway are expected to be completed in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-ypodomes_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypodomes-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The runway entered service on 11 September 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Overall, the project took almost a quarter century to build, from inception in 1997, and it has an estimated cost of \xe2\x82\xac179 million ($202 million).<sup id="cite_ref-odyssey_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odyssey-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The runway will be extended by 1000 meters into the sea, with a total length of 3440 meters and will be equipped with <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">ILS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> When the runway opens for commercial use it will be able to accommodate 89.6% of current commercial aircraft types, as opposed to just 22.6% before the extension,<sup id="cite_ref-odyssey_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odyssey-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and will improve safety while landing in bad weather conditions and low visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span \n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Between 1994 and 2010, Thessaloniki Airport saw a rise in passenger traffic equal to 76%, from 2.2 million in 1994 to 3.9 million in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-ypa.gr_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypa.gr-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Between 2003 and 2008 the airport saw a passenger traffic increase of 19.1% from 3.5 million to almost 4.2 million passengers, an all-time high. The number of passengers dropped in next years. However, over the last two years the airport experienced passenger traffic increase to just above four million by 2013. Significant traffic increase took place during 2014, with the total number of passengers exceeding the five million mark for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-ypa.gr_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ypa.gr-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_statistics">Annual statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Airport &quot;Makedonia&quot;"><img alt="Macedonia Airport" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Thessaloniki_Metro_airport.svg/15px-Thessaloniki_Metro_airport.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Thessaloniki_Metro_airport.svg/23px-Thessaloniki_Metro_airport.svg.png 1.5x, src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BSicon_bvvWSLe.svg/40px-BSicon_bvvWSLe.svg.png" decoding="async" title="bvvWSLe" width="40" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BSicon_bvvWSLe.svg/60px-BSicon_bvvWSLe.svg.png 1.5x, class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMr" colspan="2">\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding:0 3px 0 0;">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="padding:0 0 0 3px;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The airport is directly connected with the city\'s major road arteries in the southeast, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_National_Road_16" title="Greek National Road 16">EO16</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Motorway_25_(Greece)" title="Motorway 25 (Greece)">A25</a>, which connects Thessaloniki with <a href="/wiki/Chalkidiki" title="Chalkidiki">Chalkidiki</a>, via the <a href="/wiki/Greek_National_Road_67" title="Greek National Road 67">\xce\x95\xce\x9f67</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Inner_Ring_Road" title="Thessaloniki Inner Ring Road">Thessaloniki Inner Ring Road</a> provides access to the <a href="/wiki/Motorway_1_(Greece)" title="Motorway 1 (Greece)">A1</a>/<a href="/wiki/European_route_E75" title="European route E75">E75</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egnatia_Odos_(modern_road)" title="Egnatia Odos (modern road)">A2</a>/<a href="/wiki/European_route_E90" title="European route E90">E90</a> motorways. A total of 2,285 parking spaces for cars exist at the front of the terminal building. A <a href="/wiki/Car_rental" title="Car rental">car rental</a> service is available at the terminal building. In addition, taxi services are available outside the airport terminal building 24 hours a day.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are plans to connect the airport with the <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Metro" title="Thessaloniki Metro">Thessaloniki Metro</a> network, which is set to open in 2023 after delays. Attiko Metro, the company overseeing the project, has published a map of proposed extensions, and it includes an overground extension of <a href="/wiki/Line_2_(Thessaloniki_Metro)" title="Line 2 (Thessaloniki Metro)">Line 2</a> towards the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-Istoriko_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istoriko-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This extension is not an immediate concern for the company, however, since the terminus of Line 2, <a href="/wiki/Mikra_station" title="Mikra station">Mikra</a>, will be connected with the airport by a 10-minute shuttle bus.<sup id="cite_ref-synenteuksi_mylopoulou_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-synenteuksi_mylopoulou-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Detailed planning of the metro extension toward the airport was initiated in March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-line_2_tender_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-line_2_tender-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the meantime, the airport is served on a 24-hour basis by bus 01X/01N of the <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Urban_Transport_Organization" title="Thessaloniki Urban Transport Organization">Thessaloniki Urban Transport Organization</a> (OASTH), which provides bus services between the <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Bus_Station" title="Thessaloniki Bus Station">Thessaloniki Bus Station</a> (KTEL) and Makedonia airport arrivals/departures.<sup id="cite_ref-01X_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-01X-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2750" data-file-height="1554" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_Tu-154_HA-LCR_at_Thessaloniki_-_2018-04-30_-_Andy_Mabbett_-_01_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HA-LCR next to the airport fire station, in April 2018</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 12 August 1997, Olympic Airways Flight 171, a <a href="/wiki/727-200" class="mw-redirect" title="727-200">Boeing 727-230</a> registered as SX-CBI inbound from <a href="/wiki/Ellinikon_International_Airport" title="Ellinikon International Airport">Athens Ellinikon Airport</a>, touched down late and was steered off the runway to avoid overrunning into the sea. None of the 35 passengers and crew were killed, but the aircraft was damaged beyond repair.<sup id="cite_ref-OAF_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OAF-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 17 December 1997, <a href="/wiki/Aerosvit_Flight_241" title="Aerosvit Flight 241">Aerosvit Flight 241</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-42" title="Yakovlev Yak-42">Yakovlev Yak-42</a>, operating the route from <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to Thessaloniki, lost contact with the airport\'s air traffic control and during the second attempt the aircraft crashed in the <a href="/wiki/Pierian_Mountains" title="Pierian Mountains">Pierian Mountains</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Mount_Olympus" title="Mount Olympus">Mount Olympus</a>. A total of 70 people, passengers and crew, 41 of which were Greeks, were killed.</li>\n<li>On 4 July 2000, HA-LCR, a chartered <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Flight_262" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Flight 262">Mal\xc3\xa9v Flight 262</a> <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154" title="Tupolev Tu-154">Tupolev Tu-154</a> landed on its belly. The crew had forgotten to lower the undercarriage and the plane skidded 400&#160;m (1,300&#160;ft) on the runway. Thanks to the plane\'s robust construction and the engines\' high position, the plane was able to become airborne again as the pilots applied full throttle. It circled while the crew lowered the undercarriage and landed safely. There were no injuries. It was considered uneconomical to repair the aircraft. The aircraft still remains on site,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> although airline markings have been obscured and it has been heavily depleted of re-usable spares.</li>\n<li>On 15 June 2013, an AMC Airlines Boeing 737-800 on behalf of Astra Airlines Greece, registration SU-BPZ performing flight A2-921 from Novosibirsk (Russia) to Thessaloniki (Greece) with 160 passengers, landed on Thessaloniki\'s runway 16 at about 07:14L (04:14Z) but overran the end of the runway by about 110 meters/360 feet and came to a stop with all gear on soft ground. No injuries occurred, the aircraft received minor if any damage.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thessaloniki_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Greece" title="List of the busiest airports in Greece">List of the busiest airports in Greece</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Greece" title="Transport in Greece">Transport in Greece</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span
